## Overview

<span commentid="745" data-persistent-comment-id="745" class="persistentComment" style="background-color: var(--innovera-yellow100); cursor: pointer; transition: background-color 0.3s;">Avasa is developing a novel medical device to solve the high-risk, time-consuming problem of manually suturing micro-arteries. This memo informs a Series A investment decision, recommending a pass on the current terms due to a critical funding gap and unrealistic commercial projections, but suggests exploring a restructured deal contingent on hiring commercial leadership.</span>

## Strategic Opportunity Fit

Strategic Opportunity Fit – Mismatch with core thesis. While Avasa aligns with Mayfield's "Category Creator" and "People First" principles through its novel technology and strong founder, its capital-intensive, hardware-focused MedTech model falls outside the firm's primary focus on software and AI infrastructure.

## Execution Roadmap

The investment thesis requires Avasa to achieve FDA 510(k) clearance by Q2 2026 and subsequently validate surgeon adoption with its initial 12-patient clinical study \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 20\], \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 21\]. The primary execution risks are a projected capital shortfall that jeopardizes reaching these milestones and the complete absence of an in-house commercial team to execute the post-clearance launch \[CHAPTER: finance-and-operations\].

## Recommendation

Avasa is targeting a clear, unserved market for arterial couplers, created by the documented technical failure of the dominant incumbent's product in this specific application \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 9\]. The company's patented "zero-strain" mechanical solution has demonstrated 100% success in preclinical animal trials, positioning it as a first-mover to establish a new standard of care \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 18\].

## Critical Open Questions

- Can the NZ$4.75M Series A realistically fund the company to FDA clearance, given the projected NZ$7.9M burn required to reach that milestone?
- Are the revenue projections credible, given the aggressive ramp assumptions are not supported by a realistic sales capacity model or validated sales cycle data?
- How coachable is the founder, and is he willing to hire an experienced commercial leader to address the team's primary execution gap?
- What is the true defensibility of the patent portfolio, and what is the risk posed by the competitor's patent on the future Flow Doppler Sensor product?

## Tell it to me straight

> Look, this is a brilliant founder with a 10x product for a real, painful problem. That's the good news. The bad news is everything else. The TAM is fantasy, the financial model is a joke built on impossible sales numbers, and the deal is structured to run out of gas halfway to the finish line. We're being asked to fund a science project, not a business. The only way this works is if we re-price it, fund it properly to get through the FDA, and force them to hire a grown-up to run the commercial side. Otherwise, it's a hard pass.

## Six-T Risks

## Should We Do It? (Strategic Attractiveness & Fit)

**Strategic Attractiveness of the Prize:** The opportunity is to create and dominate a new medical device category for arterial coupling, a clear and unserved clinical need created by the technical failure of the market incumbent \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 9\]. While the company's claimed $30 billion Total Addressable Market (TAM) is misleading, the realistic, device-focused Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) is approximately $224 million \[CHAPTER: market-research\]. This niche market offers the potential for high gross margins, assuming the company can move beyond its currently unrealistic 97-98% projections to the still-strong industry median of \~65% \[CHAPTER: unit-economics\]. However, the most likely exit is a strategic acquisition post-regulatory clearance in the \~$200 million range, which presents a solid return but may not align with Mayfield's target for massive, venture-scale outcomes \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 29\].

**Strategic Fit with the Organization:** The venture presents a mixed fit with Mayfield's investment thesis. The founder, Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera, is a "missionary" with exceptional founder-market fit, aligning perfectly with the firm's "People First" philosophy \[CHAPTER: team-and-execution\]. Avasa's goal to establish a new standard of care also fits the "category creator" thesis \[CHAPTER: opportunity-validation\]. However, the venture is a capital-intensive hardware play with a long, multi-year path to profitability, which conflicts with Mayfield's stated aversion to such models unless they exhibit software-like recurring revenue \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 31\]. While the razor-and-blade model has recurring elements, the business is fundamentally a medical device, representing a stretch from Mayfield's core expertise in AI and enterprise software.

**Strategic Edge / Unfair Advantage:** Mayfield's primary advantage would be its "Company Building" services, particularly in recruiting a senior commercial leader to fill the team's most critical gap \[CHAPTER: team-and-execution\]. However, Mayfield lacks a strategic edge in the areas of greatest near-term risk: navigating the FDA 510(k) regulatory pathway, managing clinical trials, and building sales channels into hospital procurement systems \[CHAPTER: gtm-and-partners\], \[CHAPTER: legal-and-ip\]. A specialized MedTech investor would possess a significant unfair advantage over Mayfield in guiding the company through these critical milestones.

Should we do it? – Borderline (Medium confidence). Summary rationale: The venture pairs an ideal "missionary" founder and a category-creating vision with a business model and market size that are a significant stretch from Mayfield's core software thesis and return expectations.

## Can We Do It? (Execution Capacity & Control)

**Hard Assets (Physical/Financial Capacity):** Mayfield possesses the financial capacity to lead the investment. However, analysis reveals the proposed NZ$4.75M round is insufficient to fund the company's projected NZ$7.9M burn to its next key milestone of FDA clearance \[CHAPTER: finance-and-operations\]. To execute successfully, Mayfield would need to structure and lead a larger, properly capitalized round (e.g., NZ$8M+), which is within its financial capability but requires renegotiating the current deal terms. The firm has no relevant physical assets, such as manufacturing facilities, to contribute.

**Market Relationship (Market Access):** Mayfield has a significant execution gap in market access. The firm's network is concentrated in the enterprise software and AI ecosystems, not in the medical device sector. It lacks deep, pre-existing relationships with the key stakeholders Avasa must win over: reconstructive microsurgeons, Key Opinion Leaders (KOLs) at academic medical centers, and hospital Value Analysis Teams (VATs) \[CHAPTER: gtm-and-partners\]. Mayfield would be unable to provide meaningful customer introductions and would be entirely reliant on the founder's network, limiting its ability to actively de-risk the go-to-market plan.

**Soft Assets (People & Skills):** The firm's expertise in mentoring founders and recruiting executive talent is a strong asset that directly addresses Avasa's identified lack of commercial leadership \[CHAPTER: team-and-execution\]. However, Mayfield's team lacks the specific, hands-on domain expertise required to guide Avasa through its most critical near-term challenges: FDA regulatory strategy, clinical trial design and execution, and quality systems for medical device manufacturing \[CHAPTER: legal-and-ip\], \[CHAPTER: product-and-technology\]. In these crucial areas, Mayfield would be a passive board member, unable to provide the active, value-add mentorship that defines its model.

Can we do it? – Borderline (High confidence). Summary rationale: While Mayfield can provide the necessary capital and general company-building support, it lacks the critical domain expertise and market relationships in MedTech to effectively guide the company through its highest-risk regulatory and commercial milestones.

## Synthesis & Recommendation

The Avasa opportunity presents a fundamental conflict between Mayfield's "People First" philosophy and its core investment thesis. The venture is led by an exceptional "missionary" founder with a strong technical moat and a clear vision to create a new category—all attributes that align with Mayfield's ideal investment profile. However, the strategic attractiveness of the prize is questionable for a fund targeting massive, software-driven outcomes. The realistic market is a niche hardware segment with a likely exit via a \~$200 million acquisition, falling short of a typical Mayfield home run.

This strategic mismatch is compounded by a severe execution gap on Mayfield's side. While the firm can provide capital and general mentorship, it lacks the specific regulatory, clinical, and hospital sales expertise to be an effective partner. Investing in Avasa would mean betting on a great founder but in a game Mayfield does not know how to play. The firm would be ill-equipped to help navigate the venture's most critical risks, forcing it into a passive role that contradicts its hands-on, "company-building" model. The combination of a borderline strategic fit and a weak capacity to execute makes this a high-risk proposition for the firm.

**Recommendation: Continue Due Diligence**

Proceed with a tightly scoped, 60-day diligence plan focused on three thesis-breaking questions before making a final decision:

1. **Founder Coachability and Financial Acumen:** Can the founder acknowledge and correct the significant flaws in the financial plan, and is he willing to hire an experienced commercial leader post-investment? This directly tests the "People First" thesis.
2. **Path to Venture-Scale Returns:** Is there a credible path for Avasa to expand beyond the arterial niche and displace the incumbent in the larger venous market, creating the potential for a >$1B outcome?
3. **Syndicate Expertise:** Can a specialist MedTech venture firm be brought into the syndicate to lead diligence and provide the necessary domain expertise on the board, filling Mayfield's execution gap?

## Opportunity Validation Analysis

### Opportunity Validation

Avasa is addressing the high-risk, time-consuming, and technically difficult problem of manually suturing micro-arteries in reconstructive surgery. This procedure, the current standard of care, takes approximately 40 minutes per connection and has a failure rate of 5.6%, creating a significant clinical and economic burden \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 3\]. The opportunity is validated by strong demand signals, including a company-led survey where 89% of 100 surgeons expressed a desire for an arterial coupler \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 6\]. Further validation comes from successful preclinical trials in which Avasa's device demonstrated 100% patency in chronic ovine studies, providing foundational evidence of its technical viability before human trials \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 18\].

### Market Summary

The company's claim of a $30 billion Total Addressable Market (TAM) is misleading as it is based on the total value of surgical procedures, not device sales \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 7\]. A more realistic, device-focused Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) is approximately $224 million, which is contingent on Avasa successfully creating a new arterial coupler market of a similar size to the existing venous coupler market. The broader market for anastomosis devices is growing steadily at a CAGR of approximately 7.5%, driven by an increasing volume of complex surgeries and a systemic shift toward more efficient surgical technologies. The single most important market fact is the existence of a well-defined, unserved niche for arterial couplers, created by the documented technical failure of the dominant incumbent's product in this application \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 9\]. This validates the problem and significantly de-risks the market creation challenge.

### Competitive Landscape

<table class="border-collapse w-full" style="min-width: 75px;">
<colgroup><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"></colgroup><tbody><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Competitor / Category</p></th><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Core Strength</p></th><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Key Weakness / Gap</p></th></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Manual Suturing (Standard of Care)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Entrenched practice; no device cost; universal applicability to arteries and veins.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Slow (40+ minutes); technically difficult; high failure rate (5.6%) [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 3, 8].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Synovis (Baxter International)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Dominant market leader for venous couplers; established brand trust and global distribution.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Technology is unsuitable for arteries due to vessel stiffness, causing tears and trauma [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 9, 12].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Lydus Medical</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>First-mover advantage with an FDA 510(k) cleared device for small arteries.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Different technology (suture aid, not a coupler); clinical adoption and superiority are unproven.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Large MedTech (e.g., 3M, J&amp;J)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Massive scale in R&amp;D, manufacturing, and commercial distribution; strong hospital relationships.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>No current direct solution for arterial coupling; slower to innovate in niche segments.</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

The primary competitive challenge is displacing the entrenched manual suturing practice by demonstrating overwhelming clinical and economic value. The "White Space" for Avasa is the arterial coupler market, which exists because the dominant adjacent player, Synovis, has a technical gap that makes its product unsuitable for arteries \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 9\]. Avasa's success depends on proving its clinical superiority to manual suturing and defending its technical moat against fast-followers who may enter once the market is validated.

### Regulatory & Legal Landscape Summary

The opportunity is defined by a high but navigable regulatory barrier that functions as both a hurdle and a moat. The primary operational hurdle is securing FDA 510(k) clearance for the Avasa Coupler, which is classified as a Class II medical device \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 20\]. Avasa has a clear plan for this process, having already engaged with the FDA to validate its pathway, which de-risks the timeline. Successful clearance would create a significant barrier to entry for new, undercapitalized startups.

The venture's defensibility is rooted in its intellectual property. The core innovation is protected by pending patents in key global markets, including the USA, Europe, and China \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 16\]. This IP is supplemented by a trade secret moat around the precision manufacturing process, which requires tolerances of 20 microns \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 16\]. However, the "patent pending" status is not a guarantee of issuance, and the company faces a potential IP challenge from a competitor who holds a patent relevant to Avasa's future product pipeline (the Flow Doppler Sensor).

### Meta-Analysis: Is This a Valid Opportunity?

The opportunity is fundamentally valid but represents a niche, high-risk play. Its validity is anchored in strong external evidence of a real, painful, and unserved clinical need. The problem of arterial anastomosis is well-documented, and the market gap was created by the documented technical failure of the dominant incumbent, Synovis, to serve this segment \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 9\]. This provides a rare "white space" opportunity where Avasa can be a category creator rather than a direct challenger. Direct demand signals from surgeons, with 89% stating a desire for an arterial coupler, further validate that the company is solving a problem the market wants solved \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 6\].

However, the attractiveness of the opportunity is constrained by its scale and execution risk. The realistic market size (SAM of \~$224M) is substantial but far smaller than the company's misleading $30B TAM claim, which caps the potential for a venture-scale outcome. Furthermore, the entire opportunity is contingent on a single, binary event: achieving FDA 510(k) clearance on a specific timeline \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 20\]. While a direct competitor (Lydus Medical) is already FDA-cleared, Avasa's distinct coupler technology could still win if it proves clinically superior. In summary, the external opportunity is real and attractive because a clear market gap exists with validated customer pain, but its realization is entirely dependent on navigating a high-stakes regulatory barrier before the competitive window closes.

## Path to Success Analysis

### Product & Technology

Avasa's product path is a phased, risk-mitigated progression from a single device to a multi-product platform. The immediate focus is on achieving regulatory clearance for its core product: a three-part system comprising a disposable coupler, a handset, and a reusable applicator designed to replace manual sutures in microvascular anastomosis \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 4\]. The technology is at an advanced pre-commercial stage, with a design-frozen, pre-production unit already validated in chronic ovine studies that demonstrated 100% patency \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 17, 18\]. The critical near-term milestones are completing the required GLP animal study, submitting the FDA 510(k) application by Q3 2025, and securing clearance by Q2 2026 \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 20\].

The primary technical risks shaping this path are manufacturing scalability and a significant funding gap. The device's efficacy depends on consistently achieving 20-micron tolerances at scale with an external partner, a key operational hurdle \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 16\]. More critically, as noted in the Product & Technology chapter, the planned NZD $4.75M raise appears insufficient to cover the projected NZD $7.92M in expenses required to reach FDA clearance, jeopardizing the entire roadmap. Long-term, the path evolves into a platform strategy, leveraging the core intellectual property to launch a Flow Doppler Sensor (2027), Lymphatic Coupler (2028), and Coronary Coupler (2029), though this expansion is contingent on successfully navigating the initial product launch and securing future financing \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 23\].

### Go-to-Market

The go-to-market path is a focused, two-phase strategy that relies heavily on partnerships with clinical leaders to de-risk market entry before scaling. The initial target customer is the reconstructive microsurgeon at high-volume surgical centers, where the pain point of manual suturing is most acute \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 7\]. Phase one is a capital-efficient soft launch planned for Q3 2026, immediately following projected FDA clearance. This launch is critically dependent on a partnership model with Key Opinion Leaders (KOLs) at three pre-identified hospital sites—MD Anderson, Monash Health, and Middlemore Hospital—who will drive a 12-patient clinical study, generate validation data, and act as physician champions to navigate the hospital procurement process \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 21, 30\].

Phase two, a hard launch planned for 2028, transitions to a hybrid commercial model. This involves building a small direct sales force for major academic centers while partnering with specialized medical device distributors for broader market access \[DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. P&L – Working\]. The financial model assumes these channel partners will be compensated with 35% of revenue, indicating a clear "partner" assumption for achieving scale \[DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. P&L – Working\]. This surgeon-led, phased approach is designed to build a strong foundation of clinical evidence and advocacy to overcome the significant adoption hurdles posed by entrenched surgical techniques and complex hospital Value Analysis Teams (VATs) \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 26\].

### Revenue & Business Model

Avasa's path to revenue is based on a classic "razor-and-blade" business model, common in the medical device industry. The company will generate revenue from two distinct streams: the one-time sale of a reusable applicator instrument priced at US$3,000, and the recurring, high-volume sale of a single-use, consumable coupler, also priced at US$3,000 per unit \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 24\]. This model is designed to create a sticky customer relationship, where initial instrument placement drives a long-term stream of high-margin consumable sales tied to procedural volume.

The financial viability of this path hinges on an exceptionally high gross margin structure. The company's financial model projects gross margins of 97-98% for the consumable coupler, a figure that is a significant outlier compared to the medical device industry median of approximately 65% \[DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown\]. This margin assumption is a critical, unproven bet, further complicated by conflicting Cost of Goods Sold (COGS) data within the company's own documents, as noted in the Unit Economics chapter. The path to profitability is long, with the company's own projections not showing breakeven until 2030, reflecting the capital-intensive nature of the pre-commercial and early-launch phases \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 31\].

### Meta-Analysis: Risks & Opportunities of This Path

Avasa's strategic path is to leverage a technically superior, patent-protected device to create and dominate a new market category—arterial coupling—left open by the incumbent's product failure. The plan is to de-risk this opportunity through a capital-efficient, KOL-driven soft launch to generate definitive clinical proof. If successful, the company aims to scale using a high-margin "razor-and-blade" business model, positioning itself for a strategic acquisition. This path offers the opportunity for category creation, a key theme for Mayfield, but its execution is fraught with sequential, high-stakes risks and a potential misalignment with the firm's core investment thesis.

The success of this entire path rests on five linchpin assumptions. First, the company must secure FDA 510(k) clearance on its projected Q2 2026 timeline. Second, the compelling 100% success rate from animal trials must translate to human patients in the initial clinical study. Third, the small group of KOL partners must remain committed and prove effective at championing the device through complex hospital procurement processes. Fourth, the business model's viability depends on achieving and sustaining the projected 97-98% gross margins, an unproven and extreme outlier for the industry. Finally, the company must address the funding gap between its Series A target and the projected burn required to reach regulatory clearance, a critical flaw identified in the financial analysis.

The primary opportunity is clear: Avasa has strong founder-market fit and a validated technical solution for a well-defined, unserved clinical need. However, the path to realizing this opportunity is a gauntlet of clinical, regulatory, and commercial hurdles. The venture's success depends on flawless execution against a plan built on stacked, optimistic assumptions regarding sales velocity and margins. For Mayfield, the key vulnerability is that this is a capital-intensive MedTech hardware play, outside the firm's core software focus, with a probable M&A exit that may not deliver the venture-scale returns typically targeted. The strategic play is robust in its logic but fragile in its execution dependencies, requiring near-perfect performance at every stage to succeed.

## Operations Analysis

### Unit Economics Summary

Avasa's projected unit economics are entirely theoretical and based on a pre-revenue financial model that forecasts an exceptionally high gross margin of 97-98% for its consumable coupler \[DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown\]. This projection is an extreme outlier when compared to the medical device sector median of approximately 65% and is further undermined by conflicting internal data, with the financial model citing a Cost of Goods Sold (COGS) of $73 while the pitch deck claims $46 \[CHAPTER: unit-economics\]. The pricing strategy, which sets the consumable coupler at approximately US$3,000, is plausible as it aligns with existing competitor devices \[CHAPTER: unit-economics\]. However, the model's viability hinges on these unvalidated margin assumptions and lacks any empirical data on Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC), sales cycle length, or customer lifetime value, making the projected 2030 breakeven date highly speculative \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Financials & Operational Plan

</table>

Avasa's operational plan is centered on using a $4.75M NZD Series A to fund the company through its most critical milestone: FDA 510(k) clearance \[DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 28\]. However, a significant funding gap exists; the projected operational burn to reach this milestone is $7.9M NZD over 24 months, which exceeds the planned funding (including tax credits) and suggests a runway of only 18-19.5 months \[CHAPTER: finance-and-operations\]. The financial model also contains highly aggressive and unrealistic assumptions, projecting revenue growth to over $10M NZD in the first full year of sales (2028) with only two new sales hires, implying an unachievable per-rep productivity of over $5M NZD \[DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown\]. This mismatch between the sales capacity plan and revenue targets, combined with inconsistencies between the operational timeline and financial forecasts, indicates a high risk of the company being undercapitalized and unable to execute its post-clearance growth plan \[CHAPTER: finance-and-operations\].

### Legal & IP Constraints

The venture's operational plan is fundamentally constrained by its regulatory and intellectual property landscape. The most critical operational dependency is achieving FDA 510(k) clearance by the projected Q2 2026 date; any delay would directly impact the commercial launch timeline, extend the cash burn period, and likely necessitate additional financing \[CHAPTER: legal-and-ip\]. While Avasa's core coupler technology is protected by pending patents, a competitor's existing patent for a Flow Coupler incorporating a Doppler sensor poses a material Freedom-to-Operate (FTO) risk to the company's future product pipeline \[CHAPTER: legal-and-ip\]. This could operationally constrain Avasa's long-term growth by blocking a key future product or forcing a costly and time-consuming redesign. Furthermore, the company's proposal lacks a detailed operational plan for managing sensitive patient health information from its clinical trials, creating a compliance risk with HIPAA and GDPR that could lead to fines or trial delays \[CHAPTER: legal-and-ip\].

### Meta-Analysis: Execution Readiness, Risks & Opportunities

Avasa's execution readiness is weak. While the company has a clear operational path through regulatory clearance and a strong IP position for its core product, its financial and commercial planning is critically flawed. The venture is significantly undercapitalized for its stated plan, with a projected funding gap that threatens its ability to reach the essential FDA 510(k) clearance milestone. This financial fragility is compounded by an operational plan built on unrealistic assumptions, particularly regarding sales force productivity and market adoption speed. The projection of achieving over $10M NZD in revenue with just two sales hires in their first year is not credible and signals a fundamental disconnect between the company's technical goals and its commercial execution strategy \[CHAPTER: finance-and-operations\].

The most material operational risk is the cash runway shortfall. The projected 19.5-month runway is insufficient to cover the 24-month plan to FDA clearance, creating a near-certainty of a premature funding crisis \[CHAPTER: finance-and-operations\]. This is exacerbated by the model's stacked optimism, where any single failure—a regulatory delay, slower-than-expected sales ramp, or lower margins—could cascade and render the entire plan unachievable. Legally, the competitor patent related to the future Flow Doppler Sensor represents a significant operational constraint on the company's long-term platform vision, potentially limiting its growth trajectory even if the core product succeeds \[CHAPTER: legal-and-ip\].

Despite these substantial risks, an opportunity exists if the plan can be recalibrated. The unit economics, even if adjusted to more realistic industry-standard gross margins of 65-75% instead of the projected 98%, would still be attractive for a proprietary medical device \[CHAPTER: unit-economics\]. The primary opportunity lies in restructuring the financing and operational plan to be achievable. A properly capitalized company, focused on executing the well-defined regulatory path and building a realistic, capacity-driven go-to-market model, could successfully execute on the clear market need for an arterial coupler. The current plan, however, does not provide the economic, resource, or strategic foundation to support successful execution.

## Next Steps and Action Plan

The following action plan outlines the critical steps required to de-risk the Avasa opportunity and validate the core assumptions underpinning the investment thesis. The plan is designed to be executed over a 90-day diligence period, focusing on the most significant financial, commercial, regulatory, operational, and team-related uncertainties identified across the memorandum.

# Six T Analysis

# Chapter: 6T Risk Assessment Memorandum

### 1. Executive Risk Summary

**Overall Project Risk Profile**: This is a high-risk, high-potential medical device venture where a technically brilliant founder and a compelling product are undermined by a structurally flawed financing plan, unrealistic commercial projections, and critical gaps in the executive team.

**Top 3 Critical Risks**:

- **Inflated Market Sizing (Source: TAM)**: The company's claimed US$30 billion TAM is inflated by over 100x compared to a more realistic, device-focused SAM of US$224 million, creating a severe risk of misaligned valuation and flawed strategic planning [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 7].
- **Structurally Flawed Financing (Source: Terms)**: The NZ$4.75M Series A raise is critically insufficient to cover the company's own projected NZ$7.9M cash burn to reach FDA clearance, creating a near-certainty of a premature and highly dilutive bridge round.
- **Lack of Commercial Execution Capability (Source: Team, Traction)**: The venture is led by a technical founder with no in-house commercial leadership, and its financial model is built on "unrealistic" and "aggressive" sales projections that are disconnected from a viable go-to-market capacity plan.

**Key Mitigating Strengths**: The venture's primary assets are its founder, who has exceptional domain knowledge and founder-market fit; a core technology that offers a 10x improvement over the standard of care for a clear clinical need; and a well-defined regulatory pathway with a history of successful M&A exits for comparable companies.

**Overall Confidence in Analysis**: High. The most critical risks are identified through direct contradictions and basic errors within the company's own financial documents and pitch deck.

**Strategic Recommendation**: Do not proceed with the investment on the current terms. Propose a revised, larger deal structure that fully funds the company through FDA clearance, contingent on the founder's agreement to hire an experienced commercial leader post-close.

**The Core Decision**: Can a brilliant technical founder with a compelling product be coached to overcome critical financial planning deficiencies and build a commercially viable enterprise, and is the opportunity large enough to warrant the significant hands-on effort required?

**90-Day De-Risking Plan for Go/No-Go Decision**:

1. **Re-scope and Re-price the Round** (Owner: Corporate Development): Work with the founder to build a credible, milestone-based budget that fully funds the company to FDA 510(k) clearance and renegotiate the valuation and round size accordingly.
2. **Validate Commercial Assumptions** (Owner: Project Lead): Conduct independent interviews with 10-15 target surgeons to validate adoption intent, price sensitivity, and the perceived threat from the FDA-cleared competitor (Lydus Medical).
3. **Assess Founder Coachability and Recruiting Capability** (Owner: Project Lead): Present the findings from the financial and commercial diligence to the founder to assess openness to feedback and begin sourcing candidates for a senior commercial role to gauge recruiting potential.

### 2. The 6T Risk Matrix

software component pose a mismatch.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Medium</p></td></tr></tbody>

### 3. Deep Dive: Diagnostic Analysis & Recommended Actions

---

#### **Team: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The team is a classic example of a brilliant technical founder-led venture with a critical "Commercial Execution Gap." While founder Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera possesses exceptional domain expertise, the team lacks any in-house commercial, operational, or senior financial leadership, leading to significant blind spots. The root cause of the flawed financial projections identified in the Traction and Terms analyses is this lack of financial acumen and commercial experience on the core team.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Execution Gaps**: The current team is almost entirely technical, with no in-house commercial, regulatory, or manufacturing leadership, and an unproven ability to hire for these roles [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=qkXYDOKloJu1thNYOOjzUZg0a%2Bozr4Mtrfv1B00tpIQ%3D), p. unknown].
  - **Financial Inconsistencies**: The team's financial credibility is damaged by a "basic arithmetic error" in its use of funds, "significant discrepancies" between its pitch deck and financial model, and an understated capital need [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 28].
  - **Founder-Market Fit**: The founder and CEO has a unique combination of a first-class degree in Bioengineering and an M.D., coupled with direct experience as a Plastics Resident where he identified the clinical problem, representing exceptional founder-market fit [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 2].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: Without augmenting the team with experienced commercial and operational leadership, the venture is at high risk of failing to convert its technical innovation into a viable business.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The founder's authentic, mission-driven story and the exceptional quality of the clinical advisory board are the primary assets for recruiting senior talent.
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Make the investment contingent on the founder agreeing to a search for an experienced COO or Chief Commercial Officer with a track record in medical device market entry.
  - **Action 2**: Secure a board seat to provide active mentorship on financial planning, commercial strategy, and executive hiring.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - How coachable is the founder, and is he willing to cede operational and commercial control to an experienced executive hire?
  - Does our network have the specific MedTech commercialization expertise to effectively guide this team, or are we the wrong partner for this stage?

---

#### **TAM: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The central problem is a massively overstated market size and an underestimated competitive threat, indicating a potential lack of market analysis rigor or a deliberate attempt to inflate the opportunity. The root cause of this flawed market view is the team's miscalculation of TAM based on the total value of surgical procedures instead of the market for the device itself, as identified in the Team analysis's "Commercial Execution Gap."
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Inflated TAM**: Avasa claims a US$30 billion TAM, but the realistic, device-focused Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) is estimated at approximately US$224 million, a discrepancy of over 100x [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 7].
  - **Underestimated Competition**: The company's claim of "no direct competition" is false; Lydus Medical has already secured FDA 510(k) clearance for its Vesseal device, giving it a significant first-mover advantage [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 8].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: The vast discrepancy in market size fundamentally challenges the venture's valuation and its potential to deliver a venture-scale return.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The well-defined initial beachhead market in plastic and reconstructive surgery provides a focused entry point, and the validated exit landscape for comparable device companies offers a clear path to liquidity [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 29].
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Re-build the financial model based on the realistic US$224 million SAM to assess if a venture-scale return is still achievable.
  - **Action 2**: Conduct diligence on Lydus Medical to assess their traction, technology, and IP to better understand the competitive threat.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Is the $224M SAM large enough to support a venture-backed business, or is this a niche product better suited for a strategic acquirer post-clearance?
  - Why did the team misrepresent the TAM so significantly, and does this reflect a lack of sophistication or a lack of integrity?

---

#### **Technology: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The central problem is a critical funding gap that jeopardizes the entire product development and regulatory roadmap, despite the core technology being sound and well-validated in preclinical studies. The root cause of this issue is the flawed deal structure identified in the Terms analysis, where the capital being raised is insufficient to execute the stated technical plan.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Funding Shortfall**: The NZ$4.75M Series A raise is insufficient to cover the projected NZ$7.92M in expenses required to achieve FDA 510(k) clearance, creating a high risk of the company running out of capital before its most critical milestone.
  - **Technical Validation**: The device has been successfully validated in chronic animal (ovine) studies, which showed 100% patency, de-risking the core mechanism of action [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 17-18].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: The funding gap creates a high probability of project failure due to insolvency before the technology can be fully de-risked through regulatory clearance.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The compelling preclinical data provides a strong foundation for the FDA submission, and the 10x value proposition (80% faster procedure time) creates a strong pull for clinical trial recruitment [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 8].
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Refuse to invest on the current terms and work with the founder to structure a larger round that provides at least 18-24 months of runway, fully funding the company through FDA clearance.
  - **Action 2**: Commission a third-party manufacturing consultant to assess the scalability and quality control risks associated with achieving 20-micron tolerances with their external partner.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Are we willing to lead a larger, properly capitalized round, or does the required check size exceed our allocation for a company at this stage?
  - What is the risk that a competitor's patent on a Flow Doppler Sensor will block our ability to realize the full platform vision for this technology?

---

#### **Traction: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The venture has zero commercial traction, and its financial projections are built on a foundation of "aggressive" and "unrealistic" assumptions about sales velocity and efficiency. The root cause is the "Commercial Execution Gap" identified in the Team analysis; the R&D-focused team lacks the experience to build a credible, bottoms-up sales plan, resulting in a purely speculative growth model.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Pre-Revenue Status**: The company is pre-revenue, with first sales not projected until 2027, meaning all traction metrics are theoretical [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=qkXYDOKloJu1thNYOOjzUZg0a%2Bozr4Mtrfv1B00tpIQ%3D), p. unknown].
  - **Unrealistic Sales Ramp**: The financial model projects an exponential sales increase of over 1,100% between 2027 and 2028 (from 170 to over 2,100 units), an improbable growth rate for a new medical device entering conservative hospital systems [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=qkXYDOKloJu1thNYOOjzUZg0a%2Bozr4Mtrfv1B00tpIQ%3D), p. unknown].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: The lack of any validated commercial assumptions means the investment is a bet on a science project, not a business, with no reliable way to forecast future revenue.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The strong validation from Key Opinion Leaders (KOLs) at top-tier institutions like MD Anderson, who are committed to the soft launch, provides the most credible (though limited) form of early traction [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 30].
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: As part of diligence, conduct independent reference calls with the committed KOLs to gauge their level of conviction and understand the internal buying process at their institutions.
  - **Action 2**: Require the company to build a detailed, bottoms-up go-to-market plan for the first 12 months post-launch, including a realistic sales capacity model and CAC estimates.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Given the long sales cycles in MedTech, what is a realistic timeline to see meaningful revenue, and does that align with our fund's lifecycle?
  - How much of the "strong surgeon interest" is genuine intent to purchase versus academic curiosity, and can we validate this before investing?

---

#### **Trends: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: While the venture is well-aligned with the durable macro trend toward more efficient surgical solutions, its business model is predicated on unsustainable economic assumptions, and its market entry timing is compromised by a competitor that has already achieved regulatory clearance. The root cause of the flawed economics is the team's lack of financial rigor, as identified in the Team analysis.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Unsustainable Economics**: The financial model projects gross margins of 97-98%, a figure described as "unsubstantiated" and a significant deviation from the industry norm of \~65%, suggesting a flawed understanding of COGS [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=qkXYDOKloJu1thNYOOjzUZg0a%2Bozr4Mtrfv1B00tpIQ%3D), p. unknown].
  - **Competitive Timing**: Avasa is too late to be the first mover with a novel FDA-cleared device, as competitor Lydus Medical has already achieved this milestone, placing Avasa in a "fast follower" position.
- **C. Strategic Implication**: The combination of a competitor's head start and a potentially unviable economic model threatens the company's ability to capture the market, even if the underlying trend is favorable.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The venture's thesis is based on the sound analogy of being the "Synovis for arteries," targeting a validated market segment where the incumbent's technology failed, which is a strong strategic position [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 9].
- **Impact on Project Success**: Significant
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Mandate a third-party review of the company's COGS model and manufacturing plan to establish a realistic gross margin projection.
  - **Action 2**: Develop a market entry strategy that explicitly positions Avasa against Lydus Medical, highlighting key points of clinical differentiation.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Can a "fast follower" win in the medical device space, and what level of clinical superiority is required to displace a competitor with a multi-year head start?
  - If gross margins are closer to the industry norm of 65%, how does that impact the company's capital efficiency, future fundraising needs, and overall financial viability?

---

#### **Terms: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The central problem is that the proposed Series A deal is structurally flawed due to a material misalignment between the capital being raised and the funds required to reach the next key milestone. The root cause is a combination of the founder's financial inexperience (Team) and the resulting unrealistic projections (Traction), leading to a deal that sets the company up for failure.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Funding Gap**: The NZ$4.75M capital raise is demonstrably insufficient to cover the company's own projected cash burn of approximately NZ$7.9M to reach FDA 510(k) clearance.
  - **Inconsistent Financials**: The "Use of Funds" detailed in the pitch deck totals NZ$5.4M, which does not match the NZ$4.75M being raised, a basic arithmetic error that undermines confidence [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 28].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: Investing on the current terms would place capital at extreme risk, as the company is almost guaranteed to face a liquidity crisis before it can achieve the value-inflection milestone of FDA clearance.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The presence of credible existing institutional investors (Booster, Bridgewest, NZ Growth Capital Partners) suggests the cap table is clean and that co-investors may be willing to participate in a restructured, properly capitalized round [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A18%3A00Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A18%3A00Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=9143tg1dc1zhLXDPxRC3KkGjfFh3J1PZy6pmLkFIo3k%3D), p. 33].
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Immediately communicate to the founder that the deal is a "no-go" on current terms due to the funding gap.
  - **Action 2**: Propose leading a larger, re-priced round that provides sufficient capital (e.g., NZ$8M+) to fully fund the company through FDA clearance and initial market launch.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Are the existing investors aware of this funding gap, and what is their appetite to participate in a larger, potentially flat or down round to right-size the company's balance sheet?
  - Does the founder understand the severity of this structural issue, and is their reaction indicative of coachability or defensiveness?

---
