### Pivot Triggers & Scaling Criteria

The company has established clear conditions that would trigger a re-evaluation of its strategy, as well as the criteria required to justify scaling commercial operations.

#### Pivot Triggers

A decision to pivot or halt the GTM plan would be triggered by any of the following outcomes:

- **Clinical Failure:** Inability to meet the primary safety and efficacy endpoints in the 12-patient clinical study.
- **Regulatory Rejection:** Failure to secure FDA 510(k) clearance within 12 months of submission, indicating significant regulatory or data-related deficiencies.
- **Low Market Adoption:** An adoption rate below 15% at soft launch sites after one year, signaling weak surgeon interest or insurmountable workflow barriers.
- **Negative KOL Feedback:** Substantial negative feedback from KOLs on device performance that requires a major product redesign.

#### Scaling Criteria

A "go" decision for a hard launch and broader commercial expansion is contingent upon achieving the following milestones:

- **Regulatory Approval:** Successful receipt of FDA 510(k) clearance.
- **Clinical Validation:** Achievement of all primary and secondary endpoints from the initial clinical study.
- **Commercial Traction:** Meeting or exceeding the soft launch targets for adoption rate (30%) and revenue (\~$170k).
- **KOL Acceptance:** Confirmation from KOLs that the device is ready for broader use and can be incorporated into standard surgical protocols, a key driver of market acceptance [Intel Market Research](https://www.intelmarketresearch.com/microvascular-anastomosis-market-9100).
- **Procurement Pathway Validation:** Successful navigation of the Value Analysis Team (VAT) and procurement processes at all three pilot hospitals [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A30Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A30Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=xCSrjD0Qw95NCb85U7D3%2Fy3WyjIS%2BfQ2bhUzfrvb5Io%3D), p. 26].

## Claims

 1. The initial target customers are reconstructive microsurgeons at high-volume surgical centers.
 2. The Avasa coupler reduces arterial anastomosis procedure time by an estimated 80%.
 3. The beachhead market represents a Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) of $2.8 billion.
 4. A soft launch is planned for Q3 2026 at three KOL-led hospital sites.
 5. The device cost is covered by existing bundled Diagnosis-Related Group (DRG) reimbursement codes.
 6. A 12-patient clinical study is considered sufficient by KOLs to drive initial adoption.
 7. The company has a manufacturing agreement with Ann Tong in Taiwan, enabling gross margins above 90%.
 8. The financial model allocates 35% of revenue to distributor and contract sales costs.
 9. The Avasa Coupler requires an FDA 510(k) premarket notification for the U.S. market.
10. The consumable coupler is priced at US $3,000 per unit.

# Unit Economics

## Unit Economics

### Overview

Projected unit economics are based entirely on pre-revenue financial modeling, forecasting a gross margin of over 97% on its consumable coupler device [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A11%3A38Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A11%3A38Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=S%2BDsFeb7YWw7cSdHZ6q0Gb%2BwPLC9r9vqwJJI2Tnn0Z4%3D), p. unknown]. The model's viability is driven by three key assumptions: achieving the target Average Selling Price (ASP) of approximately US$3,000, maintaining an exceptionally low Cost of Goods Sold (COGS), and rapidly scaling unit sales through a direct and distributor sales model. Currently, none of these core economic assumptions are validated with historical or pilot data; they remain purely theoretical. The company's path to unit profitability is long, with breakeven projected for 2030, and is highly sensitive to the unproven assumptions regarding sales cycle length, customer acquisition cost, and manufacturing costs at scale [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A11%3A38Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A11%3A38Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=ERcrObK7Xh%2BEmXoFurB1D8x1hhwq%2FPQ7qS96%2Bcn5RQE%3D), p. unknown].

#### Key Takeaways

- **Exceptional but Unrealistic Margins**: The financial model projects a 97-98% gross margin, which is unsubstantiated and significantly deviates from the 65% median for the medical device sector [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A11%3A38Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A11%3A38Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=S%2BDsFeb7YWw7cSdHZ6q0Gb%2BwPLC9r9vqwJJI2Tnn0Z4%3D), p. unknown], [Mercer Capital — VALUE FOCUS](https://mercercapital.com/content/uploads/Medtech-and-Device-24Q3.pdf). This projection relies on conflicting and unverified COGS estimates.
- **Absent Customer Acquisition Data**: There is no historical or pilot data for Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC), sales cycle length, or hospital re-order rates. The entire financial forecast is built upon theoretical S&M expenses, making it impossible to assess payback periods or the true cost of scaling.

### Risks

- **Unrealistic Gross Margin Projections**: ❌ The projected 97-98% gross margin is an extreme outlier compared to industry leaders like Medtronic (65%) and sector medians (65.1%) [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A11%3A38Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A11%3A38Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=S%2BDsFeb7YWw7cSdHZ6q0Gb%2BwPLC9r9vqwJJI2Tnn0Z4%3D), p. unknown], [GuruFocus — MDT (Medtronic) Gross Margin %](https://www.gurufocus.com/term/grossmargin/MDT), [Mercer Capital — VALUE FOCUS](https://mercercapital.com/content/uploads/Medtech-and-Device-24Q3.pdf). This suggests a high risk of underestimating production costs.
- **Conflicting COGS Data**: 🚩 The financial model uses a Bill of Materials (BOM) cost of $73 for the coupler, while the pitch deck appendix cites a total cost of $46 [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A11%3A38Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A11%3A38Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=S%2BDsFeb7YWw7cSdHZ6q0Gb%2BwPLC9r9vqwJJI2Tnn0Z4%3D), p. unknown], [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A11%3A38Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A11%3A38Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=ERcrObK7Xh%2BEmXoFurB1D8x1hhwq%2FPQ7qS96%2Bcn5RQE%3D), p. unknown]. This 58% variance in foundational cost data undermines the reliability of all margin and profitability forecasts.
- **Theoretical Customer Acquisition Model**: 🚩 All CAC, LTV, and payback metrics are derived from top-down S&M spending forecasts, not from any real-world testing. The model assumes a 35% commission for distributors but lacks validation on the all-in cost to acquire, onboard, and support a new hospital account [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A11%3A38Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A11%3A38Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=S%2BDsFeb7YWw7cSdHZ6q0Gb%2BwPLC9r9vqwJJI2Tnn0Z4%3D), p. unknown].
- **Information Risk**: The analysis is constrained by a complete lack of empirical data. All key performance indicators for unit economics are projected, carrying the lowest possible confidence level. The investment decision relies entirely on accepting the management's financial model without market validation.

### Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **Verified Bill of Materials**: Obtain detailed, itemized quotes from the primary manufacturer (Ann Tong) for the coupler and applicator components to resolve the COGS discrepancy and validate margin assumptions.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Price Validation**: Conduct a formal Willingness-to-Pay (WTP) study with 5-7 hospital procurement directors and Value Analysis Team (VAT) members to validate the US$3,000 price point for both the consumable and the reusable applicator. Success is defined as confirmation that this price is acceptable within current DRG reimbursement bundles.
- **Sales Cycle Mapping**: Interview 5-10 procurement and clinical department heads at target hospitals to map the end-to-end process and timeline for new device evaluation and approval. The goal is to replace the model's implicit adoption timeline with a data-driven estimate.
- **CAC Proxy Test**: Allocate a small budget ($10k-$15k) for a 90-day targeted digital outreach campaign aimed at microsurgeons to generate initial leads. Success would be establishing a baseline Cost-per-Lead (CPL) to inform a more realistic bottom-up CAC model.

### Pricing & Revenue per Unit

**Data Coverage & Confidence:** Medium | Confidence: 3/5

**Method & Definitions:**

- The revenue model is based on a classic "razor-and-blade" approach, with two primary units:
  1. **Avasa Coupler**: A single-use, consumable implant.
  2. **Avasa Applicator**: A reusable instrument required for the procedure.
- Revenue per new hospital account will consist of initial applicator sales plus ongoing, recurring revenue from coupler sales, dependent on procedure volume.

**Results (with tags):**

- **Projected Price**: US$3,000 for the consumable Coupler and US$3,000 for the reusable Applicator [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown].
- **Projected ASP**: The financial model uses a blended Average Selling Price (ASP) for the coupler, starting at NZ$3,975 (\~US$2,425) in 2027 and declining to NZ$2,649 (\~US$1,615) by 2035 as the company enters emerging markets [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].
- **Confidence tag**: ⚠️ Plausible. The US$3,000 price point is identical to that of the competing GEM COUPLER and within the range of other microvascular couplers, which can cost between $800 and $2,500 per device [gemsynovis.com](https://gemsynovis.com/pricelist/?utm_source=openai), [24LifeSciences — Microvascular Couplers Market Outlook 2025 to 2032](https://www.24lifesciences.com/microvascular-couplers-market-market-5727).

**Reality Check & Red Flags:**

- The pricing strategy appears sound in the context of existing competitor products and reimbursement structures. The primary risk is not the price point itself, but the unvalidated assumption of the sales volume and adoption rate at this price. The deck includes a quote from a procurement director stating the price is not prohibitive, but this single data point is insufficient for validation [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown].

### COGS & Gross Margin

**Data Coverage & Confidence:** Medium | Confidence: 2/5

**Method & Definitions:**

- **Cost of Goods Sold (COGS)**: Defined as the Bill of Materials (BOM) cost for each device, including components, assembly, and sterilization.
- **Gross Margin %**: Calculated as (Revenue - COGS) / Revenue.

**Results (with tags):**

- **Projected COGS (Coupler)**: The financial model is built on a BOM cost of NZ$73 per coupler [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. However, the pitch deck appendix presents a conflicting, lower figure of NZ$46 per coupler [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown].
- **Projected Gross Margin**: Based on the NZ$73 COGS figure, the model projects a gross margin of 97-98% for the coupler throughout the forecast period [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].
- **Confidence tag**: ❌ Unrealistic.

**Reality Check & Red Flags:**

- 🚩 **COGS Discrepancy**: The 58% difference between the two stated COGS figures ($73 vs. $46) is a major red flag regarding the fidelity of the company's financial planning.
- ❌ **Extreme Margin Outlier**: A 97-98% gross margin is exceptionally high for the medical device industry. Publicly traded industry leaders report significantly lower margins: Medtronic at 65.0%, Globus Medical at 66.6%, and the sector median at 65.1% [GuruFocus — MDT (Medtronic) Gross Margin %](https://www.gurufocus.com/term/grossmargin/MDT), [GuruFocus — GMED (Globus Medical) Gross Margin %](https://www.gurufocus.com/term/grossmargin/GMED), [Mercer Capital — VALUE FOCUS](https://mercercapital.com/content/uploads/Medtech-and-Device-24Q3.pdf). While a novel product can command high margins, a figure this far above the benchmark is questionable and implies either a revolutionary, unproven manufacturing process or a significant underestimation of costs at scale.

### Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC), LTV, & Payback

**Data Coverage & Confidence:** Low | Confidence: 1/5

This analysis is in **Low-Data Mode** due to the absence of any historical or pilot data.

- **What We Know**:

  - The company is pre-revenue and has not yet acquired a customer.
  - The go-to-market strategy relies on a direct sales force, KOLs, and distributors to target hospitals [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown].
  - The financial model allocates a significant budget to Sales & Marketing, including a line item for "Distributor/Contract Sales Costs" set at 35% of revenue [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].

- **What We Don’t Know**:

  - The all-in CAC to acquire a new hospital account, including sales salaries, commissions, marketing, travel, and conference expenses.
  - The typical sales cycle length, from initial contact to VAT approval and first purchase. Industry norms suggest this can take several months [CB Insights — Movac Investments](https://www.cbinsights.com/investor/movac).
  - The Lifetime Value (LTV) of a hospital, which would depend on procedure volume, re-order rates, and potential for expansion to other departments or products.
  - The resulting CAC Payback Period.

- **Implications**:

  - The lack of CAC and sales cycle data makes the revenue ramp in the financial model entirely speculative.
  - Profitability and cash flow projections are highly sensitive to these unknown variables. A CAC that is 50% higher than implicitly modeled, or a sales cycle that is 6 months longer, would dramatically delay the projected 2030 breakeven point and increase capital requirements.

- **Targeted Data Requests**:

  1. A detailed, bottom-up CAC model showing all anticipated costs per acquired hospital.
  2. Data from clinical advisors on typical procurement timelines for similar devices in their institutions.
  3. A framework for calculating hospital LTV, including assumptions for procedure volume, account retention, and expansion revenue.

- **30–90 Day Validation Plan**:

  1. **Procurement Timeline Validation**: Interview 5-7 non-KOL hospital procurement managers to validate the assumed sales cycle. Success is a documented process map with time estimates for each stage.
  2. **Sales Cost Modeling**: Task the management team with building a detailed territory economic model for a single sales representative, including salary, commission, T&E, and support costs, against a realistic sales quota.

### Cohort Analysis

**Data Coverage & Confidence:** Low | Confidence: 1/5

This analysis is in **Low-Data Mode**.

- **What We Know**: No cohorts exist as the company is pre-revenue.
- **What We Don’t Know**: All cohort-based performance metrics, including acquisition cost, procedure ramp-up, re-order velocity, and LTV/CAC by hospital type (e.g., academic center vs. community hospital).
- **Implications**: The financial model relies on blended averages for sales growth. This can mask significant performance differences between early adopters (likely KOL-affiliated hospitals) and the broader market, leading to inaccurate forecasts as the company scales.
- **Targeted Data Requests**: A plan for how the company will measure and report on customer cohorts post-launch, including the key metrics to be tracked.
- **30–90 Day Validation Plan**: Define the metrics for the initial soft launch sites (MD Anderson, Monash, Middlemore) to be tracked as the first "Founder-Led Sales" cohort [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown].

### Sensitivity & Scenarios

**Data Coverage & Confidence:** Medium | Confidence: 2/5

The financial model includes a sensitivity analysis on how Operating Income changes based on the price of the Avasa Coupler. This analysis is supplemented with analyst-derived sensitivities on other key levers.

 4. The financial model is built upon a Bill of Materials (BOM) cost of NZ$73 per coupler.
 5. The company's pitch deck appendix states a conflicting total cost of NZ$46 for the coupler.
 6. The medical device sector median gross margin is 65.1%.
 7. The company is pre-revenue and has no historical data on Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC).
 8. The financial model assumes distributor and contract sales costs will be 35% of revenue.
 9. The company projects it will reach breakeven (positive operating income) in 2030.
10. The company's financial model shows that profitability is highly sensitive to the device's selling price.



# Finance and Operations

Projections: Complete | Model: P&L-only Assumption Book: Basic | Evidence Types: [Mgmt | Analyst] Section Confidence (1–5): 2

## Overview

This chapter assesses the financial and operational feasibility of Avasa's plan to secure a $4.75M NZD Series A round. The projections are entirely forward-looking, aiming to fund the company through FDA 510(k) clearance and a subsequent commercial launch. The analysis scrutinizes the underlying assumptions, linking capital deployment to operational milestones and testing the plan's integrity against industry benchmarks. The model indicates a path to profitability but relies on highly aggressive, unvalidated assumptions regarding market adoption and sales force productivity.

### Key Takeaways

- **Aggressive Post-Launch Growth**: The financial model projects a rapid revenue ramp to over $10M NZD in the first full year of sales (2028), driven by assumptions of swift market penetration that are not substantiated by external benchmarks or a detailed go-to-market capacity plan [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].
- **Funding Gap to Stated Runway**: The requested $4.75M NZD raise, even when combined with projected R&D tax credits, appears insufficient to cover the projected $7.9M NZD operational burn over the 24 months required to reach the key 510(k) clearance milestone, indicating a potential runway shortfall of 4-6 months [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 28], [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].

## Risks

- **Stacked Optimism**: The financial plan's success hinges on the simultaneous achievement of multiple aggressive assumptions: rapid market entry, best-in-class sales productivity from Year 1, and sustained high gross margins. A minor delay or underperformance in any single area could render the entire projection unachievable.
- **Sales Capacity Mismatch**: The model projects over $10M NZD in 2028 revenue attributed to just two new sales hires, implying a per-rep productivity of over $5M NZD in their first year [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. This is unrealistic, as medical device sales representatives typically require a 6-to-12-month ramp-up period to reach full productivity [Martal](https://martal.ca/sales-statistics-lb/).
- **Inconsistent Timelines**: Management's presentation materials indicate a soft launch in Q3 2026, but the financial model does not forecast any revenue until 2027, creating a 6-month gap and questioning the alignment between the operational roadmap and financial plan [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 30], [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].
- **Burn Rate vs.** **Runway**: The projected two-year pre-revenue burn of $7.9M NZD exceeds the planned funding of $6.45M NZD (including tax credits), suggesting the company will run out of cash before its target 3Q26 510(k) clearance date without additional capital or significant cost reductions [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].

## Next Steps

### Additional Evidence

- **Critical Information Need**: A bottom-up sales capacity model is required. This model must be built on industry-standard assumptions for sales rep ramp time (6-12 months), quota attainment, and sales cycle length (approx. 156 days for medical devices) to produce a credible revenue forecast [Martal](https://martal.ca/sales-statistics-lb/), [Medium](https://medium.com/%40archerwind/sales-roi-calculator-quantifying-deal-acceleration-client-relationship-value-through-ai-powered-fa1215a82da3).

### Derisking Actions

- **Surgeon Adoption Interviews (30 days)**: Conduct structured interviews with 5-10 target plastic surgeons (outside of existing KOLs) to validate the perceived value proposition and identify potential adoption hurdles that could lengthen the sales cycle.
- **Procurement Pathway Validation (60 days)**: Engage with 3-5 hospital procurement or Value Analysis Team members to confirm the reimbursement pathway and identify potential administrative barriers to adoption, pressure-testing the assumptions outlined in the pitch deck [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 26].
- **Recalibrate Financial Model (90 days)**: Re-forecast revenue and headcount based on findings from the sales capacity model and surgeon interviews. The revised model must explicitly link hiring dates to revenue generation, respecting realistic ramp times.

## Projection Baseline & Integrity

The financial model is a management-prepared P&L projection. All figures are **Projection** and denominated in NZD. The model assumes first revenue in 2027, following a projected 510(k) clearance in Q3 2026 [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 20], [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].

| Metric ($M NZD) | Y1 (2027) ✔ | Y2 (2028) ★ | Y3 (2029) △ | Y4 (2030) ▢ | Y5 (2031) ▢ | \*\*| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | \**| **Revenue*** \*| $0.7 | $10.5 | $25.4 | $50.9 | $102.0 | \**| **YoY Growth %*** \*| N/A | 1,414% | 143% | 101% | 100% | \**| **EBITDA*** \*| ($3.2) | ($1.8) | $0.5 | $11.1 | $31.4 | \**| **Free Cash Flow*** \*| N/A | N/A | N/A | N/A | N/A | ***Source: Analyst calculations based on [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. Note: Free Cash Flow cannot be calculated as the model is P&L-only.***

- **Break-Even (Projection):** EBITDA positive in Y3 (2029).
- **Prerequisites:** Achieving 510(k) clearance by 3Q26, hiring initial sales team in 2028, and securing rapid adoption at initial launch sites.
- **Realism:** **Unrealistic**. The revenue growth from Y1 to Y2 is exceptionally aggressive and not supported by a credible, capacity-driven sales plan.

## Key Drivers & Assumptions

The model's outcomes are highly sensitive to a few key operational and commercial assumptions.

| Driver | Y1 (2027) | Y2 (2028) | Y3 (2029) | Evidence Tag | Conf | Assessment | Rationale (1 line) | \*\*| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | \**| **New Coupler Units Sold*** *| 170 | 2,104 | 7,540 | Mgmt | 1 | Unrealistic | Assumes exponential growth with no evidence of market adoption velocity.* \*| \**| **Coupler ASP (NZD)*** *| $3,975 | $4,904 | $3,301 | Mgmt | 3 | Base | Price point is aligned with existing competitor devices for veins [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 24].* \*| \**| **Gross Margin %*** *| 98% | 98% | 98% | Mgmt | 2 | Aggressive | While high margins are possible, 98% is top-decile and assumes flawless manufacturing scaling.* \*| \**| **Sales Headcount*** *| 0 | 2 | 5 | Mgmt | 2 | Unrealistic | Hiring plan is severely misaligned with the revenue it is expected to generate.* \*| \**| **Distributor/Sales Costs (% of Rev)*** *| 35% | 35% | 35% | Mgmt | 2 | Aggressive | A fixed 35% commission is assumed, which may not hold as the company scales or enters new markets.* \*| \**| **R&D Spend ($M)*** *| $1.3 | $2.6 | $2.8 | Mgmt | 3 | Base | Spend is front-loaded for regulatory approval, which aligns with the stated strategy.* \*| ***Source: All data is Projection from [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].***

## Cash, Burn & Runway

The proposed raise does not appear sufficient to reach the primary inflection point of 510(k) clearance.

- **Proposed Raise (Projection):**\* \*$4.75M NZD [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 28] \**- **Avg Monthly Net Burn (next 24 mo):*** ***Base:*** *($330k) | **Downside:*** \*($357k) \**- **Runway:*** ***Base:*** *19.5 mo | **Downside:*** \*18 mo (Calculated as: [$4.75M raise + $1.7M tax credit] / Avg Monthly Burn) \**- **Trough Cash:*** *Occurs pre-clearance in mid-2026.- **Burn Mix (24-mo avg):*** *Headcount (49%), R&D (incl.* \*trials) (39%), G&A (12%) ***Source: Analyst calculations based on [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown] and [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 28]. Downside assumes a 10% increase in R&D and G&A costs due to unforeseen delays.***

## Capital Requirements & Use of Funds (Milestone-Linked)

The use of funds is focused on achieving regulatory clearance, but the budget appears misaligned with both the raise amount and the projected burn.

| Category | $ (NZD) | % | Milestone / Outcome (date) | \*\*| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | \**| **R&D / Product*** \*| $2.6M | 48% | V&V testing, FDA submission, patent costs for 510(k) clearance (3Q26) | \**| **G&A / Ops*** \*| $2.5M | 46% | Staff salaries, property, and business costs through the regulatory phase | \**| **S&M / GTM*** \*| $0.3M | 6% | Pre-launch marketing, KOL onboarding, and tradeshows | \**| **Working Capital Buffer*** \*| $0 | 0% | No buffer allocated | \**| **Total*** *| **$5.4M*** *| **100%*** \*| | ***Source: Projection data from [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 28]. Note: The sum of allocated funds ($5.4M) exceeds the stated raise amount ($4.75M).***

**Assessment:** The capital raise does not appear sufficient to reach the next value inflection (510(k) clearance) and preserves zero buffer for delays or unforeseen costs.

## Operational Resourcing & Capacity

The hiring plan is disconnected from revenue-generating capacity, representing a critical flaw in the operating plan.

**Hiring & Ramp (Projection)**

| Function | Current FTE | Adds by Y2 (2028) | Ramp Assumption | Evidence Tag | \*\*| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | \**| **Sales*** \*| 0 | 2 | Not specified; implied immediate full productivity | Mgmt | \**| **Product/Eng*** \*| 5 | 4 | N/A | Mgmt | \**| **Customer Support*** \*| 0 | 2 | N/A | Mgmt | \**| **G&A*** \*| 1 | 6 | N/A | Mgmt | ***Source: [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].***

**Capacity Math (Sales)**

- **Formula:** Bookings = (# AEs × Ramp % × Quota)
- **Model Implication (2028):** $10.46M Revenue = (2 AEs × 100% Ramp × $5.23M Quota)
- **Assessment:** **Unrealistic**. An annual quota over $5M NZD for a new medical device is not credible for reps in their first year, especially when industry benchmarks suggest a 6-12 month ramp-up period to achieve full productivity [Martal](https://martal.ca/sales-statistics-lb/).

## Scenario & Sensitivity Analysis

The model is highly sensitive to initial sales traction and pricing.

**Scenarios (Projection)**

- **Base:** Management plan as presented in the financial model.
- **Upside:** Assumes 20% higher unit sales and 10% higher ASP due to strong KOL endorsement.
- **Downside:** Assumes 30% lower unit sales and a 1-year delay in achieving positive EBITDA.

| Metric (End of Y2 - 2028) | Downside | Base | Upside | \*\*| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | \**| **Revenue ($M NZD)*** \*| $7.3 | $10.5 | $13.8 | \**| **EBITDA ($M NZD)*** \*| ($3.8) | ($1.8) | $0.1 | \**| **Runway (months)*** \*| N/A | N/A | N/A | ***Source: Analyst calculations based on [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. Runway is not applicable as the company is projected to be post-revenue.***

**Sensitivity (Runway Impact from Trough**)The sensitivity table in the financial model focuses on operating income based on the coupler price, showing high leverage. For example, a price drop from $3k to $2k NZD in Y3 (2029) would reduce operating income by over $6M NZD, pushing out breakeven by at least a year [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].

## Model ↔ Roadmap Alignment (next 24 months)

There are notable inconsistencies between the operational roadmap presented in the pitch deck and the timing of financial events in the model.

| Quarter | Product Events | GTM Events | Hiring/Spend | Financial Ramp Event | Alignment Check | \*\*| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | \**| **Q2 2025*** *| V&V Testing Begins | N/A | R&D spend peak ($2.8M annual) | Continued Burn | **Pass*** \*| \**| **Q3 2026*** *| 510(k) Clearance | Soft Launch (per deck) | S&M spend begins ($0.65M annual) | No revenue in model | **Fail*** \*| \**| **Q1 2027*** *| N/A | Soft Launch (per model) | N/A | First Revenue ($0.7M annual) | **Concern*** \*| ***Source: Analyst assessment based on [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 17, 30] and [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].***

## Sanity-Check Scorecard & Red Flags

**🚩 Red-Flags:**

- **Year-1 revenue without a validated sales capacity plan:** The model projects significant revenue without a realistic plan for the sales team required to generate it.
- **AE full-quota productivity 60–90 days post-hire:** The model implicitly assumes sales reps are 100% productive immediately, which is unrealistic.
- **Multi-year hockey-stick dependent on unproven channels:** The entire forecast relies on rapid, frictionless adoption in a market with established surgical procedures.

---

\*\*\*\*\*\***Final Summary Box**

- **Revenue Start:** Q1 2027 (Confidence: Low)
- **Break-Even (Projection):** EBITDA+ 2029; Cash-Flow+ (Unknown)
- **Capital to Break-Even (Projection):** $15M NZD
- **Validated Assumptions:** 1/5 • **Critical Unknowns:** Sales cycle length, surgeon adoption rate, sales rep productivity.
- **Overall Credibility:** Low
- **Key Risks:** Unrealistic sales projections, insufficient runway to key milestones, misalignment between operational and financial plans.
- **Go/No-Go Next Gate:** Secure independent validation of sales cycle and adoption rate before proceeding.

## Claims

 1. The company seeks to raise $4.75M NZD in a Series A round.
 2. Financial projections forecast first revenue in calendar year 2027.
 3. The model projects revenue will grow from $0.7M NZD in 2027 to $10.5M NZD in 2028.
 4. EBITDA breakeven is projected for 2029.
 5. The proposed funding of $4.75M NZD, plus $1.7M in tax credits, is projected to provide 19.5 months of runway.
 6. The projected operational burn over the next 24 months is approximately $7.9M NZD.
 7. The 2028 revenue target of $10.5M NZD is planned to be achieved with two sales hires.
 8. The model assumes a gross margin of approximately 98% on its coupler device.
 9. The company's pitch deck indicates a soft launch in Q3 2026, which is not reflected with revenue in the financial model until 2027.
10. The use of funds outlined in the pitch deck totals $5.4M NZD, which exceeds the stated $4.75M NZD raise amount.



# Team and Execution

## Overview

The Avasa team is led by its founder, Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera, whose dual expertise in bioengineering and medicine provides exceptional founder-market fit and technical credibility. The venture's strength is rooted in his vision, supplemented by a world-class network of clinical advisors from institutions like Stanford and MD Anderson. The team is well-positioned to navigate the MedTech regulatory and clinical landscape, demonstrating a strong grasp of the FDA 510(k) pathway. However, the team is currently a small, R&D-focused unit with significant gaps in commercial and operational leadership. The venture's success is critically dependent on the founder and the ability to execute a challenging hiring plan for specialized roles ahead of commercialization.

### Key Takeaways

- **Founder Centrality**: The venture's success is almost entirely dependent on the founder, Dr. Abeysekera, who embodies the clinical vision, technical expertise, and entrepreneurial drive. This is both a massive strength and the single greatest risk.
- **Commercialization Gap**: The team is technically proficient but lacks any in-house commercial or operational leadership. The entire go-to-market and scaling plan relies on future hires who are not yet identified.

## Risks

- **Key Person Dependency**: The venture is exceptionally reliant on founder and CEO Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera for its technical, clinical, and strategic leadership. His departure would pose an existential threat to the company.
- **Hiring Execution Risk**: The go-to-market plan requires hiring specialized, hard-to-find talent in regulatory affairs, sales, and operations on a specific timeline. Failure to attract and retain this talent could severely delay the commercial launch.
- **Founder Transition Challenge**: The founder must evolve from a clinical innovator into a commercial CEO capable of leading a scaled organization. This transition is a common failure point for technically-led startups.
- **Cultural Dilution at Scale**: The planned transition from a small, mission-driven R&D team to a larger commercial organization risks creating cultural friction and diluting the clinician-centric focus that is currently a strength.

## Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **Founder 360-Degree References**: Conduct confidential reference checks on Dr. Abeysekera with former colleagues, mentors, and early investors to validate leadership capabilities, coachability, and resilience.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Accelerate COO/CSO Search**: Immediately engage a retained executive search firm specializing in MedTech to begin the search for a COO or CSO, targeting a hire within the next six months to de-risk founder dependency.
- **Formalize Contractor Conversion Plan**: Develop and present offers to convert the two critical contract development engineers to full-time employees with equity grants to secure core technical talent ahead of the Series A close.
- **Develop Succession Scenarios**: Mandate as a board-level action for the CEO to develop and present preliminary succession scenarios for key roles within the first 90 days post-investment.
- **Map Key Advisor Commitments**: Formalize the commitments from the Key Opinion Leader (KOL) advisory board regarding their specific roles in the soft launch and clinical studies to ensure alignment and de-risk market entry.

## Core Team Composition & Roles

The current Avasa team is a small, technically-focused unit centered around the founder's clinical and engineering expertise. The core team consists of a founder/CEO, a project manager, and three development engineers (two of whom are contractors), which is consistent with the typical 2-to-5-member size for early-stage medical device startups [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=gqCHiWpncTdJlrMFKKWTKCkAA5f1l4J7J0UHqvuWwBY%3D), p. 32]. The team's composition is heavily weighted towards product development, which is appropriate for its current pre-commercial stage focused on achieving regulatory clearance.

### Key Roles and Responsibilities

The team's structure covers the essential functions of leadership, clinical validation, and technical execution, augmented by a strong external advisory network.

### Identified Gaps and Planned Hires

The primary gaps in the current team are in commercial and operational functions. The team lacks dedicated, in-house leadership for business development, sales, marketing, manufacturing scale-up, and regulatory affairs. This lean, R&D-focused structure presents a risk as the company approaches commercialization, a challenge further detailed in the *Talent Risks & Retention Strategy* section.

The company's financial model acknowledges these gaps and outlines a hiring plan to address them, as detailed in the *Talent Sourcing & Development Strategy*. Key planned hires include:

- **Executive Leadership:** A COO/CSO role is planned to be filled starting in FY2026 [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. P&L – Working].
- **Regulatory & Quality:** A full-time RAQA (Regulatory Affairs/Quality Assurance) Manager is slated for hire in FY2025, a critical role for managing the FDA submission and post-market compliance [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. P&L – Working]. This is particularly important as medtech startups often face challenges acquiring talent with specialized regulatory expertise.
- **Commercial Team:** The plan includes adding a Business Development/Product Manager in FY2026, followed by Marketing and Sales staff in subsequent years to support the product launch [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. P&L – Working].

While the hiring plan is defined, the execution of sourcing and onboarding this specialized talent remains a key challenge for the next phase of the company's growth.

## Innovation Capability Assessment

The Avasa team's innovation capability is evaluated based on its demonstrated entrepreneurial skills, technical competence, fluency in navigating the medical technology ecosystem, learning velocity, and the strength of its professional network. The assessment indicates a team with a strong, founder-led capacity to execute, though this capability is heavily concentrated in its principal, creating the key person dependency discussed in *Talent Risks & Retention Strategy*.

### Entrepreneurial Skills

The team exhibits strong foundational entrepreneurial skills, centered on the founder's direct experience with the clinical problem.

- **Problem-Driven Foundation**: Founder Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera identified the procedural challenges of microvascular surgery during his residency as a plastic surgeon and felt "compelled to develop a solution" [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 2]. He subsequently left his clinical practice in 2018 to establish Avasa, demonstrating a commitment to solving a problem he personally encountered.
- **Customer Development**: The team has validated the clinical need through interviews with 100 surgeons, finding that 89% desire an arterial coupler [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 6]. This direct engagement with the target market from an early stage indicates a robust customer development process.
- **Early Venture Validation**: The company's trajectory was shaped by its participation in the VentureLab incubator program after winning the 2018 Velocity $100K Challenge, suggesting an early adoption of structured venture-building practices.

### Technical Competence

Avasa's technical capabilities appear robust, anchored by the founder's unique qualifications and validated by tangible product development milestones.

- **Founder's Dual Expertise**: Dr. Abeysekera possesses a first-class degree in Bioengineering alongside his medical degree, a combination that provides deep insight into both the clinical application and the engineering requirements of the device [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 2, 32].
- **Demonstrated Execution**: The team has progressed from concept to a complete pre-production unit, having successfully conducted proof-of-concept, feasibility, and chronic animal studies [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 17].
- **Preclinical Validation**: The device has been validated in ovine studies (n=17 vessels), achieving 100% patency with no thrombosis, leaks, or mechanical failures observed in chronic trials [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 18]. A successful live animal study on a pig's femoral artery further substantiates these findings.

### MedTech Ecosystem Fluency

The team demonstrates a sophisticated understanding of the complex MedTech environment, including regulatory, clinical, and procurement pathways.

- **Regulatory Navigation**: Avasa has established and validated a clear FDA 510(k) pathway for its device, having secured confirmations from the agency on its Class 2 designation and key study parameters [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 20].
- **Procurement and Reimbursement Acumen**: The team has mapped the hospital procurement process, identifying the Value Analysis Team (VAT) as the key decision-making body and understanding the established DRG bundled payment model used by competitor Synovis [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 25, 26]. This awareness is critical for market access.
- **Clinical Trial Design**: The plan for an initial investigator-led clinical study is well-defined, with clear objectives, endpoints, and a low-risk profile that aligns with the standard of care for the target patient population [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 21].

### Learning Velocity and Adaptability

Avasa has shown an ability to systematically test hypotheses and de-risk its technology through an iterative process. The progression from initial concept to a design-frozen, pre-production unit validated in multiple animal studies indicates a methodical approach to learning and development [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 17]. The company's early success in the Velocity challenge and subsequent participation in an incubator program suggest a capacity for rapid learning and adaptation within a structured innovation framework.

### Network Strength

The team's primary strength lies in its extensive and high-quality external network of clinical advisors and investors.

- **Key Opinion Leader (KOL) Engagement**: Avasa has assembled a world-class advisory board of senior plastic surgeons from leading institutions, including Stanford, Harvard, and MD Anderson [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 22].
- **Committed Clinical Partners**: Crucially, these KOLs are not passive advisors; they are committed to leading the product's soft launch at their respective institutions, providing immediate access to influential first users [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 30].
- **Investor Validation**: The company is backed by a syndicate of established venture firms, including NZ Growth Capital Partners and Pacific Channel, which validates the team's capabilities and provides access to additional resources and networks [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 33].

### Capability Summary

The following table summarizes the innovation capability assessment for the Avasa team.

## Talent Sourcing & Development Strategy

Avasa's talent strategy is centered on a phased approach: maintaining a lean, technically-focused core team through regulatory clearance, followed by a rapid commercial expansion post-market approval. The plan relies heavily on external hiring to fill specialized commercial and operational roles, augmented by an established network of clinical advisors.

### Phased Hiring Plan

The company's hiring roadmap is directly tied to its product development and market entry milestones, prioritizing capital efficiency before scaling revenue-generating functions [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. The plan addresses key functional areas required for a medical device launch, consistent with industry benchmarks for cross-functional teams that include R&D, quality assurance, and regulatory affairs.

The hiring strategy is divided into two distinct phases detailed below.

<table class="border-collapse w-full" style="min-width: 75px;">
<colgroup><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"></colgroup><tbody><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Phase & Timeline</p></th><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Key Roles to Hire</p></th><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Strategic Rationale</p></th></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Phase 1: Pre-Launch (2025-2026)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>QA Engineer, Business Development / Product Manager</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>This phase focuses on securing regulatory clearance and preparing for market entry. The addition of a QA Engineer is critical for supporting the existing RAQA Manager through the 510(k) submission process [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. Hiring a Business Development/Product Manager in 2026 is essential for refining the go-to-market strategy and engaging with initial launch sites ahead of the planned 3Q26 soft launch [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 30].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Phase 2: Commercial Scale-Up (2027 onwards)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Production Engineer, Sales, Marketing Manager, Customer Support, Operations Staff</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Following projected 510(k) clearance, the focus shifts to commercial execution. This phase involves a significant expansion of headcount to build out sales, marketing, and support functions necessary to drive adoption and manage customer relationships [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. The medical device industry faces a talent shortage in specialized roles like regulatory affairs, with average time-to-hire reaching 60-90 days, a factor that must be incorporated into the operational timeline.</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

### Advisory Network & Partner Resources

Avasa's primary strategic asset is its network of world-class Key Opinion Leaders (KOLs) in plastic surgery, with advisors from institutions including MD Anderson, Stanford, and Harvard [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 22]. This network is not only critical for clinical validation and trial execution but also serves as a powerful channel for market access and surgeon-led procurement advocacy. These KOLs are already committed to championing the soft launch, which significantly de-risks initial market penetration [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 26].

For execution, the company currently uses contract engineers to maintain flexibility in its R&D function [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 32]. To manage the planned commercial expansion, Avasa should consider engaging specialized medical device recruitment firms to accelerate the hiring of sales and marketing personnel, a common strategy for rapid team build-outs in the sector.

### Talent Development & Upskilling

The current core team is predominantly technical, composed of the founder, engineers, and a project manager [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. 32]. A key development priority is to build commercial and market-facing competencies within this group to ensure engineering decisions remain aligned with customer needs.

The most critical development path is that of the founder, Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera. His transition from a clinical innovator to a commercial CEO will be essential for scaling the business post-launch. This involves developing skills in sales leadership, strategic finance, and organizational management. For all new commercial hires, an intensive onboarding program will be required to ensure a deep understanding of the device's clinical application, technical differentiation, and the procedural workflow it aims to replace.

## Team Structure & Governance

The proposed organizational structure for Avasa is designed to evolve from a lean, research-focused entity into a functional commercial organization. Governance will transition from founder-led decision-making to a formal board-driven model, balancing operational autonomy with investor oversight.

### Organizational Model & Reporting Structure

Avasa currently operates with a flat, founder-led structure centered on its CEO, Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown]. The core team is small, consistent with early-stage medtech ventures where a size of two to five members is common.

The company's financial model outlines a phased expansion of this structure, contingent on funding and market entry milestones. The hiring plan projects growth from approximately six full-time equivalents (FTEs) in 2025 to over 80 by 2038, building out dedicated functions for Sales, Marketing, Operations, and Customer Support alongside the core R&D and G&A teams [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown]. This planned evolution aligns with industry benchmarks that emphasize the need for multidisciplinary teams—including R&D, marketing, clinical, and operations—to successfully bring a medical device to market.

Post-investment, governance will be formalized through the establishment of a Board of Directors, where investors will hold representation. The CEO will report directly to this board. This structure is standard for venture-backed companies and provides a necessary framework for strategic oversight, accountability, and mentorship.

### Decision Rights & Autonomy

Decision-making authority will be formally delineated between the management team and the new Board of Directors.

- **Board of Directors' Authority**: The board will oversee major strategic and financial decisions. This includes approving annual budgets and major capital expenditures, authorizing future financing rounds, ratifying key executive hires, and approving any potential merger or acquisition events.
- **CEO & Management Authority**: The CEO will retain operational autonomy to execute the approved strategy. This includes managing the product development roadmap, overseeing the regulatory submission process, directing the commercial launch, managing the team on a day-to-day basis, and making operational spending decisions within the approved budget.

This division ensures the founding team has the necessary freedom to operate and meet milestones, while the board provides critical governance and holds management accountable for performance.

### Key Integration Points & Communication

The team's success depends on managing several critical external integration points. Communication protocols will be established to ensure timely and accurate information flow to key stakeholders.

- **Clinical & KOL Network**: The team will work directly with Key Opinion Leaders (KOLs) and clinical trial sites, such as MD Anderson Cancer Center, to execute the planned 12-patient study and support the soft launch [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown]. This requires a structured communication plan managed by the clinical and product management functions.
- **Regulatory Bodies**: The Regulatory Affairs/Quality Assurance (RAQA) Manager will be the primary liaison with the FDA and other international regulatory bodies [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].
- **Manufacturing & Supply Chain**: Close integration with the contract manufacturer in Taiwan is essential for scaling production while maintaining quality standards [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown].
- **Board & Investors**: Formal communication will occur through quarterly board meetings with comprehensive reporting packages. Monthly investor updates will provide more frequent progress reports on key metrics.

### Performance Metrics & Milestones

Performance will be measured against a clear set of milestones tied to the two-year runway provided by the Series A investment. These metrics are divided into pre- and post-commercialization phases.

## Team Dynamics & Culture

### Leadership Style & Vision

The leadership at Avasa is centered around its founder and CEO, Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera, whose personal and professional experience directly shapes the company's culture. Dr. Abeysekera's motivation stems from his time as a plastics resident, where he identified the clinical need for a better micro-arterial connection method and felt "compelled to develop a solution" [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown]. This origin story, validated by external sources detailing his establishment of Avasa in 2018 to solve this specific surgical challenge, points to a mission-driven leadership style rather than a purely commercial one.

His dual qualifications as a medical doctor and a bioengineer suggest a leadership approach that integrates deep clinical empathy with technical pragmatism. This combination likely fosters a collaborative environment where product development is rigorously guided by real-world surgical needs. The company's vision is therefore not just to build a device, but to redefine a standard of care, a narrative that is likely to inspire and empower a team working on a technically demanding product.

### Team Chemistry & Work Style

The current core team is small and technically focused, which is appropriate for a pre-commercial medical device company. The key relationship appears to be between Dr. Abeysekera and co-inventor A/Prof. Jon Mathy, a dynamic that embeds a crucial clinician-engineer feedback loop at the heart of the company [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown]. This structure aligns with medtech industry best practices, which emphasize the value of cross-functional contributions from the earliest stages of development.

The team's work style appears methodical and milestone-oriented. They have progressed from concept to a preproduction unit validated in chronic animal studies, indicating a disciplined, iterative development process [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown]. The reliance on contract development engineers suggests a capital-efficient and flexible work style. However, as the company scales according to its financial plan—projecting growth from under 10 to over 80 employees—maintaining cultural cohesion and integrating new commercial roles (sales, marketing) with the R&D-centric core will be a significant challenge [DOC: Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx, p. unknown].

### Risk Tolerance & Cultural Alignment

Avasa's culture demonstrates a calculated balance of high technical risk tolerance with a conservative approach to clinical and regulatory risk. The team has undertaken the ambitious goal of creating an arterial coupler, a problem that the market incumbent, Synovis, failed to solve [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown]. This willingness to tackle a known, difficult technical challenge indicates a high tolerance for product development risk and a culture that values engineering breakthroughs.

Conversely, the company's methodical progression through animal studies and its detailed mapping of the FDA 510(k) pathway suggest a culture that respects regulatory discipline and the need for robust clinical evidence [DOC: 250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf, p. unknown]. This alignment with the rigorous demands of the medical device industry is critical. The company's persistence since its 2018 founding in an industry with a high failure rate further suggests a resilient culture accustomed to long development cycles and ambiguity. The primary cultural risk lies in transitioning this focused, R&D-driven dynamic to a broader commercial organization without losing its core mission-driven and clinician-centric ethos.

## Talent Risks & Retention Strategy

The primary talent-related risks for Avasa center on its significant dependence on the founder, the challenge of scaling a specialized team in a competitive market, and the cultural pressures associated with a long development cycle. A summary of these risks and their proposed mitigation strategies is presented below, followed by a detailed analysis.

border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Prioritize the hiring of a Chief Operating Officer (COO) or Chief Strategy Officer (CSO) to distribute leadership responsibilities and begin systematic knowledge transfer.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Talent Retention and Scaling</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>The current team is small, relies on contract engineers for development, and faces an aggressive hiring plan for specialized roles in a competitive medtech talent market.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Convert critical contractors to full-time employees with equity-based incentives. Implement a phased hiring plan that prioritizes roles essential for near-term regulatory and clinical milestones.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Succession Planning</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>No clear successor for the CEO or other critical technical roles has been identified, which amplifies the key person risk.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>The board should mandate the development of a formal succession plan. The planned COO/CSO hire should be assessed for long-term leadership potential and succession readiness.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Culture and Burnout</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>The extended pre-revenue development timeline, initiated in 2018, creates a risk of team burnout. The planned transition to a commercial entity could cause a culture clash between the R&D team and new commercial hires.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Establish clear, milestone-based incentives to maintain team motivation through the pre-launch phase. Proactively define and manage the company's culture to integrate new functions without diluting the core mission.</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

### Key Person Risk

Avasa exhibits an extreme concentration of risk in its founder, Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera. He is the CEO, inventor of the core technology, and the primary clinical visionary who identified the market need from his experience as a surgeon [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=gqCHiWpncTdJlrMFKKWTKCkAA5f1l4J7J0UHqvuWwBY%3D), p. 2, 32]. As detailed in the *Innovation Capability Assessment*, his unique background is central to the company's strengths. Dr. Abeysekera left his surgical practice in 2018 to dedicate himself to the venture, demonstrating a high level of commitment but also consolidating critical institutional knowledge. The company's relationships with its extensive network of Key Opinion Leaders (KOLs) also appear to be centered on him [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=gqCHiWpncTdJlrMFKKWTKCkAA5f1l4J7J0UHqvuWwBY%3D), p. 22]. The departure or incapacitation of Dr. Abeysekera would present a critical, and likely existential, threat to the company. To mitigate this, the plan to hire a COO/CSO/Executive, as outlined in the financial model, must be a top priority to de-risk operations and begin distributing leadership functions [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=dfaU87qO6ho1GRFrbbPFYdRx3k4VzF%2BvhglTZFbFSaU%3D), p. unknown].

### Retention and Scaling Risk

The current team is lean, comprising the founder, a project manager, and a few engineers, two of whom are contractors [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=gqCHiWpncTdJlrMFKKWTKCkAA5f1l4J7J0UHqvuWwBY%3D), p. 32]. This reliance on contract staff for core development creates a retention risk that could delay product milestones. Furthermore, the company's financial model projects an aggressive scaling of headcount from approximately six full-time equivalents in 2025 to over 80 by 2038, introducing significant new roles in sales, marketing, and regulatory affairs [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=dfaU87qO6ho1GRFrbbPFYdRx3k4VzF%2BvhglTZFbFSaU%3D), p. unknown]. Medical device startups face notable challenges in acquiring specialized talent, particularly in regulatory compliance and clinical development, making this planned expansion a considerable risk. A formal retention strategy, including converting key contractors to full-time employees with equity incentives, is necessary.

### Succession and Governance

There is no identified successor for the CEO role or other critical technical positions. The co-inventor, A/Prof. Jon Mathy, is a key clinical advisor but his operational involvement is not specified, suggesting he is not part of the day-to-day management team [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=gqCHiWpncTdJlrMFKKWTKCkAA5f1l4J7J0UHqvuWwBY%3D), p. 32]. The lack of a clear second-in-command exacerbates the key person risk. While the financial model budgets for a senior executive hire, this position is currently vacant [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=dfaU87qO6ho1GRFrbbPFYdRx3k4VzF%2BvhglTZFbFSaU%3D), p. unknown]. A key task for the board post-investment will be to work with the CEO to develop a succession plan and ensure that the incoming COO/CSO has the potential to assume greater leadership responsibilities over time.

### Culture and Integration Risk

The company faces cultural risks stemming from its long development timeline and planned transition into a commercial organization. Avasa was incorporated in 2018, and its first product launch is not anticipated until 2026 [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=gqCHiWpncTdJlrMFKKWTKCkAA5f1l4J7J0UHqvuWwBY%3D), p. 17]. This eight-year pre-revenue period is consistent with industry norms but creates a risk of burnout for the small, mission-driven team. As the company scales post-launch, it must integrate sales, marketing, and support functions into its existing R&D-centric culture [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A13%3A04Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A13%3A04Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=dfaU87qO6ho1GRFrbbPFYdRx3k4VzF%2BvhglTZFbFSaU%3D), p. unknown], a challenge noted in the *Team Dynamics & Culture* section. This transition requires deliberate management to prevent friction between the original team and new, commercially-focused hires. Implementing clear, milestone-based incentives can help maintain motivation, while strong leadership will be required to build a cohesive culture that balances innovation with commercial execution.

## Claims

 1. The founder and CEO, Dr. Nandoun Abeysekera, possesses dual qualifications in Bioengineering and Medicine.
 2. The current core team consists of a CEO, a project manager, and three development engineers, two of whom are contractors.
 3. The company has validated clinical need with 100 surgeons, 89% of whom desire an arterial coupler.
 4. The team lacks in-house leadership for business development, sales, marketing, and manufacturing scale-up.
 5. A hiring plan is in place to add a full-time RAQA Manager in FY2025 and a COO/CSO in FY2026.
 6. The device achieved 100% patency with no critical failures in chronic ovine studies across 17 vessels.
 7. Avasa has an established advisory network of five senior plastic surgeons from institutions including MD Anderson, Stanford, and Harvard.
 8. The venture is highly dependent on its founder for its technical, clinical, and strategic leadership.
 9. The company was founded in 2018 and projects its first product launch for the third quarter of 2026.
10. The company has a validated FDA 510(k) pathway for its device and has received confirmation on its Class 2 designation.
