# Legal and IP

## Overview

Avasa's legal and intellectual property strategy is centered on its patent-pending coupler mechanism and a clear regulatory pathway. The company has filed patents in key markets and identified its manufacturing process as a trade secret. However, the competitive IP landscape is active, with a competitor holding a patent relevant to Avasa's future product pipeline. The venture's primary operational hurdle is securing FDA 510(k) clearance, for which it has a detailed plan. A notable gap exists in the stated strategy for managing sensitive patient health information from clinical trials, which will require robust compliance protocols for HIPAA and GDPR.

### Key Takeaways

- **Critical Fact 1**: Regulatory approval is the primary gatekeeper for market entry. Avasa has a clear, pre-vetted plan to navigate the FDA 510(k) process for its Class II medical device, which substantially de-risks the commercialization timeline.
- **Critical Fact 2**: The venture's long-term defensibility faces a potential IP challenge. While its core coupler is patent-pending, a direct competitor holds a patent for a technology integral to Avasa's future product pipeline—the Flow Doppler Sensor.

## Risks

- **IP Infringement**: A competitor's existing patent for a Flow Coupler incorporating a Doppler sensor presents a material risk to Avasa's product pipeline, potentially blocking or forcing a redesign of a key future offering.
- **Regulatory Delay**: The business model is entirely dependent on achieving FDA 510(k) clearance by the projected Q2 2026 date. Any delays in clinical trials or the FDA review process would postpone revenue and likely require additional capital.
- **Data Compliance Failure**: The current proposal lacks a detailed strategy for handling sensitive patient health information (PHI), creating a compliance risk with mandatory regulations like HIPAA and GDPR that could result in significant fines or trial delays.
- **Patent Rejection**: The "patent pending" status of the core technology is not a guarantee of issuance. A failure to secure a granted patent with a broad scope would significantly weaken the company's primary competitive moat.

## Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **Independent FTO Analysis**: Commission a formal Freedom to Operate (FTO) analysis from third-party IP counsel to validate the company's internal findings and specifically assess the risk posed by competitor patents to the future Flow Doppler Sensor.
- **Data Governance Plan**: Request documentation outlining the specific protocols and safeguards for collecting, storing, and processing patient health information (PHI) in compliance with HIPAA and GDPR for the upcoming clinical trial.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Regulatory Pre-Submission Review**: Engage a regulatory consultant to conduct a thorough review of the planned 510(k) submission package to proactively identify and address potential deficiencies before filing with the FDA.
- **Patent Prosecution Update**: Obtain a formal status update from Avasa's patent counsel on the prosecution of its pending applications to assess the probability, timing, and potential scope of a patent grant.
- **Preliminary Compliance Framework**: Develop a foundational data privacy and security framework for the initial clinical trial, outlining key technical and administrative controls required for HIPAA and GDPR.

## Potential Intellectual Property (IP) Considerations

Based on Avasa's proposal and supporting documents, the company's intellectual property is positioned as a core asset and primary differentiator.

### Potential for New IP Creation

The proposed Avasa Coupler's design appears to have the potential to generate new intellectual property. The core innovation centers on a novel mechanism for everting a blood vessel with minimal strain, a key limitation of existing devices when used on arteries [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 15]. Specific features that form the basis of this IP include the combination of inwardly angled, hooked pins and a movable bushing that pushes all pins outward in a single motion [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 13].

Beyond the core device patents, the company suggests that its precision manufacturing process, which requires tolerances of 20 microns, constitutes a trade secret, adding another layer of potential IP protection [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 16]. The company's product pipeline, which includes a Flow Doppler Sensor, Lymphatic Coupler, and Coronary Coupler, indicates a strategy for continued IP generation in adjacent applications [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 23].

However, the patent landscape for microvascular couplers is active, with existing patents for various anastomosis devices and methods [Google Patents](https://patents.google.com/patent/US20110106119A1/en), [Google Patents](https://patents.google.com/patent/US20140081415A1/en). Notably, competitor Synovis holds a patent for a Flow Coupler that incorporates a Doppler sensor, which is relevant to Avasa's future product pipeline [BioSpace](https://www.biospace.com/synovis-life-technologies-inc-receives-u-s-patent-for-flow-coupler).

### Leveraging Existing Corporate IP

The provided documents do not mention leveraging any pre-existing corporate IP from external entities. The intellectual property appears to be originally developed within the company by its founders, including co-inventor A/Prof. Jon Mathy [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 22].

### Stated IP Protection Considerations

Avasa states that its core technology is "Patent Pending" and that national patent applications have been filed in key strategic markets, including the USA, Europe, China, Japan, and Korea [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 16]. The company also claims that two internal Freedom to Operate (FTO) searches have been conducted with no concerns identified [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 16].

The company's commitment to ongoing IP protection is supported by its financial planning. The Series A budget allocates a portion of its $2.6M NZD R&D funds for "Existing patent filing related costs" and to "File new patents" [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 28]. Furthermore, the financial model includes a dedicated annual budget for "Intellectual Property" expenses, starting at $40K NZD and increasing to $75K NZD [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=NDdW8r67ishDTVKp%2BRQyYpxFeUDatokIb1tuPJLjzo8%3D), p. unknown].

### Consultation with Corporate IP Team

The venture proposal does not explicitly mention plans to consult with a specific corporate IP team. However, the company demonstrates active management of its IP portfolio through its patent filing strategy and dedicated budget allocations.

### Preliminary Assessment of Potential IP

Avasa's strategy is heavily reliant on the defensibility of its novel coupler mechanism. The company has taken appropriate initial steps by filing for patent protection in major global markets. The assertion of having conducted FTO searches is a positive signal, though this is a company claim and not an independent legal opinion.

Given the active patent landscape for vascular couplers, a formal, independent FTO analysis by specialist IP counsel would be an essential step in due diligence before investment. Particular attention should be paid to Avasa's planned Flow Doppler Sensor, as a competitor already holds a patent for a similar integrated technology [BioSpace](https://www.biospace.com/synovis-life-technologies-inc-receives-u-s-patent-for-flow-coupler).

## Data Usage, Privacy & Third-Party Dependency Considerations

Based on the Avasa proposal and supporting documents:

### Data Usage Profile

The venture's operations will involve processing sensitive patient health information (PHI) derived from clinical trials. The initial investigator-led study plans to enroll 12 patients to evaluate the device's safety and performance in breast free flap reconstructive surgery [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 21]. Data collected will include primary endpoints such as conversion to sutures, mechanical failures, clots, leaks, and re-operations, as well as secondary endpoints like anastomosis completion time and surgeon usability feedback [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 21].

The company's future product pipeline includes a "Flow Doppler Sensor" for real-time blood flow monitoring, which would generate an additional stream of sensitive, real-time patient data [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 23]. As noted in the *Potential Intellectual Property (IP) Considerations* section, this future product may face challenges from existing competitor patents. The provided materials do not explicitly detail measures for handling sensitive patient data or ensuring compliance with regulations such as HIPAA in the U.S. or GDPR in Europe, which are key target markets [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=NDdW8r67ishDTVKp%2BRQyYpxFeUDatokIb1tuPJLjzo8%3D), p. unknown].

### Third-Party Dependencies

The Avasa Coupler is presented as a purely mechanical device, and the available documents do not explicitly mention any dependencies on third-party data, software, or technology platforms for the core product's functionality [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. unknown].

The financial model includes a line item for "Technology and Data Costs," but it lacks the detail required to identify specific software or service dependencies [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=NDdW8r67ishDTVKp%2BRQyYpxFeUDatokIb1tuPJLjzo8%3D), p. unknown]. The future development of the Flow Doppler Sensor may introduce dependencies on embedded software, which could include third-party or open-source components, but this is not addressed in the current materials [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 23].

### Stated Considerations & Consultations

The venture proposal provides limited detail on data usage and privacy measures. The documents do not explicitly discuss data privacy impact assessments, specific security protocols for handling PHI, or a strategy for complying with relevant data protection regulations in target markets. Furthermore, there is no mention of planned consultations with IT Security, Data Governance, or specialized legal counsel regarding data handling or privacy compliance at this stage.

### Preliminary Assessment of Data & Third-Party Considerations

The venture's necessary use of sensitive patient data from clinical trials is a significant operational component that requires robust governance. The absence of a stated data privacy and security strategy is a notable gap. Given the plan to enter U.S. and European markets, compliance with regulations like HIPAA and GDPR will be mandatory for clinical trials and any future data-generating products.

If the venture proceeds, clarification and review of these aspects by relevant experts would be important. Early consultation with legal counsel specializing in health data privacy is advisable to ensure compliant protocols are established before initiating clinical studies. Additionally, should the future Flow Doppler Sensor incorporate third-party or open-source software, its licensing terms would need review by legal counsel to ensure compatibility with the company's commercial and IP objectives.

## Potential Future Regulatory or Compliance Considerations

Based on Avasa's provided materials, the venture operates entirely within the highly regulated medical device industry, making regulatory compliance a central operational requirement.

### Potential for Future Regulated Application

The Avasa Coupler is a medical device intended for surgical use, placing it directly under the jurisdiction of national and international health authorities [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 20]. The company's regulatory plan, confirmed with the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA), classifies the product as a Class II medical device [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 20], [FDA](https://www.fda.gov/medical-devices/device-advice-comprehensive-regulatory-assistance/overview-device-regulation). The company's financial model outlines a global expansion strategy, which will subject the device to the regulatory frameworks of each target market, including the United States, Europe, Japan, and China [DOC: [Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=NDdW8r67ishDTVKp%2BRQyYpxFeUDatokIb1tuPJLjzo8%3D), p. P&L – Working].

### Anticipated Future Regulatory/Compliance Landscape

Avasa's ability to commercialize is contingent on securing approvals from multiple regulatory bodies. The key compliance frameworks identified are:

### Proposed Future Consultation

The provided documents do not explicitly mention plans for future consultation with specific legal or compliance departments. However, the company's direct engagement with the FDA and detailed mapping of the 510(k) process strongly imply the involvement of regulatory specialists or consultants [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 20].

### Preliminary Assessment of Future Regulatory Needs

Avasa has proactively identified and planned for its most immediate and critical regulatory hurdle: FDA 510(k) clearance in the United States. The company's awareness of the process and timeline appears robust. A significant de-risking factor is the selection of a manufacturing partner that is already ISO 13485 accredited, which will be essential for meeting the FDA's upcoming QMSR and for entering other global markets [DOC: [250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2649/250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-19T20%3A12%3A15Z&se=2027-11-20T08%3A12%3A15Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=U91ScOJOXv0k1nP8llZRYVsiAZJnAidiSBuBu12BPVk%3D), p. 36]. The primary future challenges will be the successful execution of the 510(k) submission on the stated timeline and subsequently navigating the complex and distinct regulatory requirements of each planned international market, particularly the EU.

## Overall Preliminary Legal/IP Assessment & Key Future Considerations

**Preliminary Assessment of Potential Considerations (Based on Venture Proposal):**

Based on the Avasa proposal, the concept presents opportunities for novel IP creation through its unique coupler mechanism and proprietary manufacturing processes. The venture operates within the heavily regulated medical device sector and involves the use of sensitive patient health information, which will require careful handling and strict compliance. The company demonstrates a strong awareness of its regulatory obligations with the FDA and has taken initial steps to protect its IP. However, potential IP conflicts with existing patents and a lack of detail on data privacy protocols are key areas requiring further attention. This assessment is preliminary and based solely on the provided concept information.

**Key Future Legal/IP Consultation Points (If Venture Proceeds):**

If Avasa progresses beyond this initial concept stage, proactive consultation with relevant legal and compliance experts would be advisable on the following:

**Intellectual Property:**

- Formal, independent Freedom to Operate (FTO) review by specialist IP counsel to assess risks, particularly concerning the future Flow Doppler Sensor product.
- Guidance on maintaining trade secret protection for the company's precision manufacturing processes.
- Ongoing strategic review of the patent prosecution process to ensure the broadest possible protection is secured.

**Data Handling & Privacy:**

- Review by legal counsel specializing in health data privacy regarding the proposed collection, storage, and use of patient health information (PHI) to ensure alignment with HIPAA, GDPR, and other applicable regulations.
- Consultation with IT security experts on implementing appropriate technical and administrative safeguards for all patient data processed or stored by the company.

**Third-Party Components & Agreements:**

- Legal review of any third-party software licenses (especially open-source components) or API terms of use that may be incorporated into future products like the Flow Doppler Sensor to ensure compliance and avoid unintended IP encumbrances.

**Regulatory & Compliance (Future Scope):**

- Continued engagement with regulatory consultants to ensure the successful preparation and submission of the FDA 510(k) application.
- As the company expands internationally, consultation with legal and regulatory experts in each target market (e.g., Europe, Japan, China) will be necessary to navigate distinct approval processes.

**Conclusion & Recommendation for Internal Consultation:**

The Avasa concept presents several areas where proactive legal and IP guidance will be critical to success. Early and ongoing engagement with specialized external counsel for IP, data privacy, and regulatory matters is strongly recommended to ensure the venture protects its assets, aligns with global compliance standards, and mitigates potential risks.

## Claims

 1. Avasa's core technology is "Patent Pending" with applications filed in the USA, Europe, China, Japan, and Korea.
 2. The company's precision manufacturing process, requiring 20-micron tolerances, is considered a trade secret.
 3. Two internal Freedom to Operate (FTO) searches have been conducted by the company with no concerns identified.
 4. Competitor Synovis holds a patent for a Flow Coupler that incorporates a Doppler sensor.
 5. The venture's operations will involve processing sensitive patient health information (PHI) from clinical trials.
 6. The Avasa Coupler is classified as a Class II medical device requiring FDA 510(k) clearance.
 7. The company targets an FDA 510(k) submission in Q3 2025 and projects clearance in Q2 2026.
 8. Avasa's manufacturing partner is ISO 13485 accredited.
 9. The financial model allocates an annual budget for "Intellectual Property" expenses, starting at $40K NZD.
10. The company's product pipeline includes a Flow Doppler Sensor, a Lymphatic Coupler, and a Coronary Coupler.

# Financial Numbers - Appendix

### 1. Overview

This analysis scrutinizes the claims presented in Avasa's Series A pitch deck (`250317_Avasa_Series_A_4.75M_Deck_Extended.pdf`) and the accompanying financial model (`Avasa_Financial_Model___out.xlsx`). The overall assessment is that the company's foundational claims regarding its team, core technology, intellectual property, and regulatory pathway are generally accurate and well-supported by external evidence. However, the company's projections for market size, revenue growth, and market adoption are highly optimistic and border on stretching the definition of the addressable market. A notable discrepancy in the cost of goods was also identified between the pitch deck and financial model.

---

### 4. Red Flags & Discrepancies

1. **Inflated Total Addressable Market (TAM)**

   - **Concern**: The claim of a $30Bn TAM is disconnected from the reality of the core microsurgery market, which is estimated to be in the low single-digit billions. This suggests a misleading representation of the immediate opportunity to inflate the company's perceived scale.
   - **Diligence Question**:\
     "Can you provide the bottoms-up calculation for the $30Bn TAM and specify which markets and procedures are included? Please also detail the assumptions used to derive the $2.8Bn SAM."

2. **Highly Optimistic Financial Projections**

   - **Concern**: Projecting revenue growth to over $116M NZD within five years of launch assumes a near-flawless commercial execution and an adoption rate that is exceptionally rare for a new medical device displacing an entrenched surgical technique. This forecast carries a high risk of being unachievable.
   - **Diligence Question**:\
     "What are the key adoption rate and sales cycle assumptions underpinning the revenue ramp to $116M NZD by 2031? Can you provide case studies of comparable medical devices that achieved this growth rate post-launch?"

3. **Inconsistent Cost of Goods (COGS) Data**

   - **Concern**: The pitch deck claims a COGS of $46 for the coupler, while the financial model uses $73. This discrepancy, while small in absolute terms, is a 58% difference that calls into question the diligence behind the financial modeling and the reliability of the 90% gross margin claim.
   - **Diligence Question**:\
     "Please clarify the discrepancy in the coupler's cost of goods between the pitch deck ($46) and the financial model ($73). Which figure is accurate, and how does it impact the gross margin projections?"

4. **Reliance on Unverified Internal Data for Key Claims**

   - **Concern**: Foundational claims that support the investment thesis, such as the 100% success rate in preclinical trials and the 89% surgeon demand from an internal survey, cannot be independently verified. The investment case rests heavily on accepting this proprietary data at face value.
   - **Diligence Question**:\
     "Can you provide the full, unredacted report from the preclinical ovine study and the detailed methodology, questionnaire, and raw data from the surgeon market survey for our review?"
